: Interrogation Research Division
SUBJECT: AMCLEVE/15 - - IDEN A
IRD #72501
201-300985
BACKGROUND:
Subject is a 40-year-old PBRUMEN male who has been of continuing
WOFIRM interest since initial contact with JMWAVE and more recently
with the Caracas Station as a penetration of the IDEN B organization.
PURPOSE/PROCEDURE:
Subject was SGSWIR Led at the request of the Caracas Station because
of several issues which tended to question Subject's bona fides, possible
affiliation with PBRUMEN intelligence through relatives, unreported associ-
ation with gangster elements, thefts from WOFIRM, plus other items specified
in questions listed below. The interview was conducted in the home of
Ossar C. KALJUNG is both English and Spanish. (Subject's English is quite
good, however, during actual testing Spanish was used to avoid ambiguity or
misunderstanding of the question content.) KALBING did the translating.
RESULTS:
Subject remains sensitive to one question which is related to his past
dealings with IDEN C but in fairness to Subject this sensitivity is believed
generated by genuine uncertainity over the amount of items which he had
been instrumental in getting for IDEN C. Sensitivity; initially recorded in
other areas was resolved through post-test discussion and responses to all
other questions are regarded as substantially truthful. Subject was most
cooperative and candid throughout the entire interview.
DETAILS:
Because of the numerous issues which were believed in need of clarifi-
cation, a three phase test was structured prior to the interview and rehearsed
with Subject completely before any testing took place. Discussicns, as noted,
were in both English and Spanish. Specific questions asked of Subject and
answers given by him are as follows:

CS-COPY
1.1. - 30045


14/20/2000
Page 2
IRD 072501
Have you used any name besides IDEN A? Answer: No, except
for nicknames and allases used with WOFIRM.
Have you ever travelled to Washington, D. C.7 Answer: Yes.
Once several years ago.
Have you ever been to the Soviet Union? Answer: No.
Are any of your relatives members of the Communist Party?
After some discussion Subject felt it probable that they were.
Those specifically mentioned were his two brothers IDEN D
asd IDEN-E and also possibly a sister named IDEN F who is
also in PBRUMEN and married to a Captain in the Millia.
When the question was prefaced with the words: "Is it your
belief that any of your relatives are members, " Subject's
answer was always yes. He based this belief on the fact that
both brothers hold highly responsible positions in key industries
in PBRUMEN and hence must be members. He also noted that
prior to his leaving PBRUMEN, he (Subject) and his work brothers
were in the same way. He was a member of the President
from Subject's. As for his brother IDEN E, Subject regarded
him as the "brain" in the family and originally a very religious
person who attended Catholic services daily. He later evinced
distrust for the clergy in PBRUMEN and blamed them for the
downfall of the church. When Castro made his move, IDEN E
was in complete sympathy with him and remained with him
despite his apparent convencive to Communism, although
IDEN E never acknowledged that he had been a Communist and
would usually restrict with a comment that he (IDEN E) was a
member.
Are any of your relatives working for PBRUMEN intelligence?
His answer was that he felt that at least one of them was accord-
ing to what KALBING inferred during his discussion with Subject
the day before the SCSWIRL test. This was his brother IDEN D,
but he also wondered about his brother IDEN E who might also be
with PBRUMEN intelligence because according to what his mother
mentioned in a letter some time ago, IDEN E had been in the
USSR receiving training of some sort. This training lasted for
a full year and occurred in 1962 to the best of Subject's memory.
Subject was reac-mably sure of this date because of the "Hissile
crials" and President Kennedy's death which occurred later.

After this discussion the question read: "Is it probable that
your relatives (brothers) are working for PBRUMEN intelli-
gence? Answer: Yes."
Did you know your brother (IDEN D) was working with IDEN G
before we told you? Answer: No. But again had some
suspicious.
Besides the letters we asked you to send to your brothers have
you communicated with anyone in PBRUMEN? Answer: Yes.
His mother about two or three times a year and with an aunt
named IDEN H which was the person to whom he actually
addressed the letter to his brother which WOFIRM asked him
to write. This letter incidentally was posted in 1967 (as few
years) and the other two were not the same. The letter was
Station files. Since arrival in Caracas, Subject has written
his mother only once and had the letter posted from Miami to
prevent anyone knowing his exact whereabouts. (In addition
to these contacts, Subject has sent one telegram to his mother
soon after the IDEN I just to let her know he was alright.) I
was about this time that IDEN E wrote to him and criticized
his participation in IDEN I.
Have you seen either of your brothers since 1961? Subject answered
no. Last saw IDEN E at the airport in the distance but there
were employees from IDEN E's place of employment present
and IDEN E was apparently reluctant to go near the plane. Since
1961 Subject has not seen any member of his family and as time
goes on dues not mise them as much. The persons he claims to
have been closest to were his aunt and grandmother and addresses
comments to them personally when he does write to his mother.
When further discussing his brothers in this question, Subject
was somewhat complimentary despite their differing political
ways and generally considered them as hard-working energetic
types and their goodshools records.
Do you have a secret means of contacting anyone in PBRUMEN?
Claims be knows of friends who have used telegrams to transmit
coded messages but he has never engaged in such activity. These
messages were directed against the PBRUMEN.

Have you ever been a member of any Communist guerrilla group?
Answer: No. Later explained sensitivity to the question as
smanating from current work with two former Communist
guerrillas named IDEN K and IDEN L both of whom are now
with IDEN B.
Have you told anyone in PBRUMEN that you are working with
WOFIRM? Answer: No. This question led to a discussion
of broadcasts from PBRUMEN which identified Subject as a
member of WOFIRM. These broadcasts occurred in October
1967 according to Subject and the man figuring him was
IDEN M. The latter was not officially in Subject's WOFIRM
and the man was not actually in the same way. The other
know why it was that he was specifically named. When it was
later suggested that this announcement would probably have
come effect on his family, Subject said he just didn't know
what effect it would have and has heard of none. He agreed
that it was quite ironic that one side of the family was working
with an intelligence service which was diametrically opposed
to the side to which another member of the same family was
affiliated and in fact because of his present IDEN B employment
he was actually in the business of hunting them down. Subject
agreed that it was indeed ironic but felt his convictions differed
from the same way.
Have you told anyone in IDEN N that you are working for WOFIRM?
Noked that some knew of his past affiliation base the question
was qualified to mean his present affiliation. Later after
reactions were recorded, Subject noted that his wife is fully
writing of his WOFIRM employment as is IDEN o. He also
mentioned that a PBRUMEN type, IDEN P, whom be knows
from childhood has been Midding him constantly in Carcasa

that he is still with WOFIRM until Subject finally told him in
an offhand way. 'Sare I'm with WOFIRM," but he does not
know what effect this had on IDEN P or whether he has told
anyone of his suspicions of Subject's WOFIRM involvement.
He specifically denied that anyone other than these thres
persons were knowledgeable.
Does anyone in IDEN B know you have this meeting with us today?
Answer: No.
Have you ever been asked to perform any task or mission against
the LNHARP? Answer: No.
Have you ever performed any task or mission on behalf of IDEN G?
Answer: No.
Has anyone told or instructed you on what to report to us? Answer:
No.
Have you had contact with IDEN C since 1957? Answer: No. Con-
mend questions to this question which necessitated a break.
down test to isolate the reason for his sensitivity to the topic.
He repeatedly denied that he had had any contact with IDEN C
since the IDEN Q told him not to but acknowledged a physical
revelusion to the mention of the man's name, and a long dis-
cussion ensued regarding the extent of Subject's involvement
with the man. Subject contended that the contact began quite
innocently in 1965 and was what Subject initially thought was a
deliberate provocation to see what Subject's reaction would be.
Subject immediately reported the contact to JMWAVE handiers
and the other hand of the man's name. The first report was
IDEN Q. Subject was instructed to sell IDEN C "sellersers" (gues
with slicencers attached-about six or seven to the sent of his
recollection) in order to find out his true identity. Subject fur-
nished physical descriptions and license numbers to JMWAVE
and continued to report on contact with IDEN C. He offered
Subject $500 US which JMWAVE told Subject to keep since it was
merely a bonus given him for his work as an intermediary.
IDEN C continued to force contact with Subject and once came
to. his home in ports and made veiled threats which were
answered with counter threats of violence from Subject, and an
outright threat that Subject would kill IDEN C If he threatened

him again. In 1967 while with the IDEN R, Subject gave
IDEN C some "pencils" to keep him away which Subject did
not then report to WOFIRM but later did. He gave him about
120 altogether. Subject had promised IDEN C some 500 pounds
of C/4 explosives, M-2's, sub-machine guns, etc. but all was
intended to bait IDEN C for arrest and none was over supplied
to him. Later Subject noted after reacting to a break-down
question that he had supplied him with pencils, silencere, and
the other. The question of the question was that he would
be a matter of record with JMWAVE. The grenades were
typical military type and numbered about 24 to 48 altogether.
Again, however, Subject noted that he acted only as intermediary
between IDEN C and another individual who is now deceased in
PBRIUMEN and did not physically handle any muoritions shipments.
As noted above, continued sensitivity to the question of the amounts
or types of equipment furnished IDEN C is believed attributable
to uncertainty of Subject's part as to exactly what he did arrange
for shipment to IDEN C. As to the basic question about contact
with him since 1967 (or when he was told by IDEN C to so longer
to be the first time for the PCP, Subject insisted that he never re-
established contact or kind but always checks at IDEN 8 to
determine if IDEN C is a result.
Do you now have in your possession any arms, munitions or articles
of demolition which was once the property of the LNHARP? Only
those items which were discussed during a pre-test debriefing,
via., items brought to Caracas by him in a suitcase and consist-
ing of the following: 3 or 4 smoke grenades; 6 or 7 booby traps
(army type); 1 piece of delay pause about 100 feet long; ore primer
cord about 100 feet; 2 or 3 MK2 grenades; about 10 pencils (some
regular open market supply items and some of the "company"
name of the 100 feet) and 200 feet (200 feet) or 300 feet (200
viewer worth about $50 used). These items he said were taken
while with the IDEN R and with the knowledge of IDEN T although
IDEN T did not know exactly what he had taken. Subject was using
these items frequently in training courses and they were not to
the best of Subject's knowledge the property of LNHARP at that
time although it is possible that same of these items were at one
time LNHARP and possibly WOFIRM items. But he explained
further that these items are plentiful in the Miami area and can

easily be obtained through gun deniers. During a later conver-

in California and in Miami, but he denied being personally
involved in any such dealings.
Have you ever stolen equipment of any type from WOFIRM? Answer:
Yes. About 5 gallons of gas once from a launch boat. Other than
this, nothing.
Do you know the identities of persons who stole arms and equipment
from LNHARP? Answer: No.
Break-down questions dealing with IDEN C:
Did you have contact with IDEN C from 1965 through 1967? Answer:
Yes.
During this time did he give you $500 for equipment which he wanted?
Answer: Yes.
Did you receive more than $500 from him? Answer: No.
Is it correct that you received threats from him? Answer: Yes.
Besides the pencils, silencers, grenades and pentolite did you give
him any other items? Answer: No. (as noted continued semi-
tivity which is unexplained except in the examiner's conclusions)
Did IDEN C tell you to stop contacting him in October or November
1967? Answer: Yes.
Did you contact IDEN C after November 1967? Answer: No. (Slight
sensitivity but explained as relating to constant checking on his
whereabouts to avoid contact.)
Has your employer contacted him since November 1967? Answer:
No, not to his knowledge. On this question Subject noted that his
employer can easily obtain guns and supplies from European

sources cheaper than LNHARP. Also Subject noted that the
few.guns (small callore snub base weapons) which he has

he breaks no laws in bringing them with him on the few trips
he has made between 1967 and the present. He feels he has
been brought a clear of 6 such small sidearms to Corcesa
and also the most. This (AR-15) which he was asked to bring

was not automatic per person.
The only other items which Subject could think of which could
lias WOFRK with his organization are the silencers which he
reported on in Mizani some months back which his organisation
took from captured guerrillas and which were probably issued
to a group which west to PRURMEN and were lost. Subject is
positive they were WOFIRK issue but purportedly the serial
numbers which he submitted could not be checked.
One additional item which was cleared up dealt with the potential
which had been reported seen in Caracas. Subject voluntarily
mentioned that he had seen such a supply under the bed of a friend.
The supply was attached to magnets which were to be used to
attach the charge to the underside of a ship in Caribbean waters
of IDEN V or IDEN W naticnality. The charge was to discourage
further shipments between these latter IDENs and PRURMEN.
Subject said he detached the magnets from the penaltita and
intended using it in training ciceses for students with his present
employee. The person who brought it to Caracas was IDEN X.
Subject does not know how he got it here, but knows that his
employer could facilitate such deliveries.

SUBJECT: Letter sont to R answers from Venczuela by Luis POSADA carriles.
SOURCE: Augusto PINEDA (mat. unk.).
SUB-SOURCE: Aguedo LUGO (mat. unk.).
1. On 22 May 1968 I-111 obtained the following information
from Augusto PINEDA (mat. unk.).
2. On 19 May 1968 PINEDA was visited at home by Aguedo LUGO
(mat. unk.) who had returned from a trip to Venezuela.
3. During their conversation, LUGO showed to PINEDA a photos-
tatic copy of a lotter which had been sent from Venczuela by Luis
POSADA Carriles to Augusto VALDES Miranda, aka "Polo MIRANDA, " a
RECE leader. LUGO had delivered this letter to VALDES Miranda by
hand.
4. At a moment when LUGO was not looking, PINEDA took the
photostatic copy of this letter, which is attached to this report.
In this lotter POSADA mentioned the following matters:
a. The aid which had been given to the Association of
Bay of Pigs Veterans (Brigade 2506) by the Venczuelan Army and
the reasons why this aid was stopped.
b. Possibility of the Ministry of Defense and Ministry
of Interior of becoming involved in a plan to help Cuban oxiles
fight against the Castro regime.
c. RICE should do everything possible so that RECE will
be the Cuban exile organization to receive this aid (see preceding
paragraph 4.b.), with POSADA offering to help RECE in this respect.
MICROFILMED
JUN 7

Donr friend Palo,
This is the third letter that I am sending you. Since I am
sending this letter by messenger, I can explain more.
The Government here assisted a group of Cubans called the
Zrigade. The Department of Defense (Arny) provided this assistance
without consulting the Ministry of the Interior. When the Minister of
tie Interior found out, he demanded an explanation from the military
men and they stopped the assistance.
There are strong possibilities that a plan will be developed for
Cuba, which will involve the Ministry of Defense and the Ministry of
the Interior and which will be assigned to a group of serious persons.
I believe it is highly important that I go to Miami urgently or that
some of you come here. This is urgent.
If you vant ne to go, send my fare to this address:
San Juan Bosco Avenue
Mayflower Bldg. Apt 26
Altemira, Caracas Venezuela
On the other hand, KRISTO FERMANDEZ is being summoned by Congress.
Fe is accused of being too severe with the Comuniste. Send a telegram
as socn as possible, expressing solidarity with his attitude, in the
name of the Cubans in EXEC. If possible, mention me in the telegram.
The address is: Folice Headquarters
Las Colírea AV, las Bribas Bldg
Los Chaguarracos, Caracas, Venezuela

SUMMARY: AN INTENSIVE INVESTIGATION BY THE
DIRECTORATE GENERAL OF POLICE (D IGEPCL) ON CUBAN EXILE
FLANS TO LAUNCH AN ATTACK ON CUBA HAS REVEALED THAT
MEWERS OF THE VENEZUELAN MILITARY, WITH THE KNOWLEDGE
OF THE MINISTER OF DEFENSE, ARE DEEPLY INVOLVED. THE
VENEZUELANs HAVE PROCURED ARMS FOR THE PLOTTERS AND HAVE
HELPED THEM SRING IN ARMS BY BOAT. THE PLANNED ATTACK HAS
SEEN CANCELLED BECAUSE DIEPCL'S INVESTIGATION HAS REVEALED
DETAILS OF THE OPERATION. HOWEVER, THE MINISTRY OF DEFENSE
INTENDS TO CONTINUE TO INTEREST ITSELF IN AIDING CUBAN
EXILE PLANS. END SUMMARY.
1. IN FEBRUARY 1958, THE DIRECTORATE GENERAL OF POLICE
(DIGEPL) BEGAN AN INVESTIGATION OF REPORTS THAT VENEZUELANS
WERE PROCUR ING ARMS FOR A CUBAN EXILE GROUP IN VENEZUELA
WHICH PLANNED TO ATTACK CUBA. INITIAL REPORTS IDENT IFIED
TWO CUSANS INVOLVED IN THE CASE: SALVADOR ROMANT-ORUE-GARCIA, WHO
ARRIVED IN VENEZUELA AS AN EXILE FROM CUBA IN 1959, AND
REINALDO BONIFACIO GONZALEZ-LEON GARCIA, WHO IS A CLOSE
FRIEND OF ROLANDO MASFERRER AND WHO TOOK PART IN THE BAY

2. BY APRIL 1968 DIE POL'S INTENSIVE INVEST IGAT ION
HAD IDENTIFIED NINE MORE CUBAN PARTICIPANTS AND HAD REVEALED
THAT TWO UNIDENTIFIED MEMBERS OF THE VENEZUELAN MILITARY,
AN ARMY COLONEL AND A MAJOR, WERE DEEPLY INVOLVED IN THE
PLAN. THE TWO VENEZUELANs HAD PROCURED ARMS FOR THE GROUP
AND HAD ALSO HELPED TO ARRANGE THE ARRIVAL IN VENEZUELA IN
EARLY 195S OF TWO BOATS CARRYING ARMS. THE BOATS
WERE DOCKED AT CLU3 PUERTO AZUL AND AT PUERTO CABELLO.
3. UPON LEARNING THAT THE VENEZUELAN MILITARY WAS
ACT IVELY INVOLVED IN THE PLAN AND THAT THE MINISTER, OF
DEFENSE RAMON FLORENCIO GOMEZ KNEW THAT VENEZUELAN
MILITARY AID WAS BEING GIVEN TO THE CUBAN PLOTTERS, THE
MINISTRY OF INTERIOR CONFRONTED THE MINISTRY OF DEFENSE
ON 23 APR IL WITH THE ACCUMULATED EVIDENCE COLLECTED ON
THE CASE. THE MINISTRY OF DEFENSE ACMITTED ITS INVOLVEMENT.

1. Purwarded herewith are copies of seven foldere which
comprise the notes taken by Barrio Camella at a guerrilla
course he attended in Cuba from December 1966 through October
1967. Copies of these notes, including from unilateral
penetration agent of CIRACEROUS.
The following information carefully Many on explosive, with
the first three volumes being devoted to it exclusively.
Volumes 4 and 6 are also mostly on employees, with the first
part of each being on photography and Marriess, respectively.
Volumes 5 and 7 deal with such subjects as tradeverart, infil-
tration-affiltration operations, security. safehouses, re-
curitaments, sabotages operations, etc.
3. No copies of the attachments are being sent to
JEA/VE; we dofor to Headquarters as to whether it would be
cortinelle to reprint eons of the courses for distribution
to BREAUS or others.

CINACAS INFO DIRCATOR
FRUMEN ANSHADY
1. ON 5 FEBRUARY 1968 SUSTAVO (ORTIZ) FAEZ CONTACTED
ANTHADY-1 IN MIAMI. ORTIZ ONTRODUÇLD MINSELF AS EMPLOYED
JY CIGEPOL. HE TOLD AMSHADY-1 THAT INSURGENCY IS NOW
BUILDING UP IN URBAN AREAS AND WITHIN THE UNIVERSITIES
1. VENEZUELA AND THAT CUBANS ARE INVOLVED. HE SAID THAT
CIGEPOL HAS INFORMATION THAT CAPTAIN LESTER RODRIGUEZ AND
COMANDANTE TONY CASTELLS, BOTH OF THE CUBAN RISEI ARMY,
Anc IN VENEZUZLA OR CN ROUTE THERE FROM CUBA. HE ADDED
THAT THE PROBABLE COORDINATOR OF THE URBAN TERRORISM IS
A VENEZUELAN WOMAN WHO IS USING THE VAR NAME SUSANA BUT
THAT DIGEPOL HAS BEEN UNABLE TO IDENTIFY HER FURTHER.
2. ORTIZ SAID THAT HE WAS TO BE IN MIAMI ONLY A SHORT
WHILE AND HE WANTED FROM AMSHADY-1 WHATEVER INFO SHE HAD
AOR COULD GET ON CURRENT CUBAN INVOLVENT IN INSURGENCY
11 VENEZUELA. HE ALSO SAID THAT DIGEPOL WAS PLANNING TO
THAIN SELECTED UNIVERSITY STUDENTS, INCLUDING FEMALES, AS
PENETRATION AGENTS AND HE ASKED AMSHADY-1 IF SHE WOULD BE
SECRET


140000
PAGE-2 JNNAVE 1213 S E C R E T
IMTURESTED IN GOING TO VENEZULLA, TEMPORARILY AT LEAST,
AS A TRAINER.
3. ANSHADY-1 MADE IT CLEAR TO THE JNWAVE CASE OFFICER
THAT SHE IS WILLING TO COOPERATÉ IN ANY WAY WITH LEGITIMATE
EFFORTS TO THWART CUBAN SPONSORED INSURGENCY INCLUDING THE
POSSIBILITY OF TRIPS TO VENEZUELA AND ELSEWHERE ON TRAINING
MISSIONS. SHE REPORTED THAT SHE TOLD ORTIZ THAT SHE NAD
NO NEd INFORMATION CONCERNING CUBANS IN VENEZUELA AND SAID
SHE HAD NEITHER ACCEPTED NOR REJECTED THE TRAINING OFFER,
WHICH SHE FELT TO BE MERELY TENTATIVE. SHE DID AGREE, NOW-
EVER, TO KEEP IN TOUCH WITH ORTIZ FOR WHICH PURPOSE ME GAVE
AMSHADY-I A POST OFFICE BOX NUMBER, HIS ADDRESS AND TELEPHONE
NUMBER IN CARACAS.
4. JNNAVE REQUEST ADDELS COMMENTS ON THIS DEVELOPMENT
AND ANY INDICATION OF OPS INTEREST IN AMSHADY-1 COLLAORA-
TION WITH DIEGPOL ALONG THESE LINE3.
S E C R E T

MEMORANDUM FOR: Chief, CI/OA
SUBJECT
: Luis Clemente POSADA Carriles 201-300985
1. It is requested that a Provisional Operation
Approval be granted for the use of subject as a penetration
agent into DIG-POU and the Remberto VACITZERUI Bruzual
organization. The Caracas Station has requested that
processing be carried out.
The Caracas Station has reviewed Subject's file
and the documents sent by Headquarters and sees nothing
that would preclude the use of Subject as a penetration
of DIG-POU. (copy attached).
3. Significant information in Subject's file concerns
his two brothers who are currently in Cuba and his relations
with a well known Miami gangster. One brother, Roberto
POSADA Carriles, a suspect DSE official, is the Cuban
American American Association of the American American
Havana City. Subject has not seen either brother since
he left Cuba in 1961. Subject has also been in contact
with a well known gangster. "Lefty" Rosenthal in the Miami
area. Both JHWAVE and the FDI were aware of this contact
which was maintained at the latter's request.
B. Tuckerdanos

PAGE 2 CARACAS 3 E C R E T
SEE NOTHING PRECLUDING AMCLEVE-15'S USE AS PENETRATION
CIRASAL REQUEST POA 9E EXPEDITED.
S E C R E T *flected
:


as a source of information on subversive peronalities made available
to him thru the course of his official duties in DIEPECL.
as a penetration agent into DIGETCL and the Renterto UZCATEGUI Bruzual
intelligence organisation.


NOTES
1. In a Spanish questionnaire of Personal Information made
out in 1961, Subject listed his brother Raul POSADA-Carriles as
an administrator of the Narianao Electric Company as a relative
in some government service. He did not list his brother Roberto
in this section, although he did list Roberto in Para 16,
Subject: Brothers and Sisters.
2. In another signed but undated Spanish Personnel
Information form of apparently 1965, he again listed both his
brothers in Section N. Subject: Brothers and Sisters, and in
Section N he again listed his brother Raul, who he stated he
believed to be working for the Cuban government as an engineer.
He again failed to list his brother Roberto.
3. Concerning his PRQ Part I filled out in March 1965, again
no mention of his brother Roberto appears in Section XIV, Subject:
Relatives, Acquaintances and Contacts. in any Government Service.
4. According to POSADA's own admission in an LC Flutter
of 14 April 1965, he had been involved in planning for a
Guatemalan coup headed by Roberto ALEJOS-Arzu. This matter later
came to the attention of the FBI. There is an FBI report dated
17 May 1965 in the 201. AMCLEVE-15 also furnished information
on this Guatemalan coup for JMWAVE, who disseminated this
information in July 1965.
5. AMCLEVE-15 informed JMWAVE concerning other independent
exile operations into Cuba in July of 1965.
6. His PRQ Part II. Section XI, dated September 1965, says
that "Subject is of good character, very reliable and security


conscious. Subject demonstrated good security techniques while
reporting on the activities" of Roberto ALEJOS concerning the
attempted coup against Guatemala.
7. An FBI report of 30 September 1965 outlines the contacts
that had been made by some Americans seeking to purchase pistols,
blasting caps, hand gernades and silencers. This is the first
indication in the 201 that Subject was involved with Frank
Lang "Lefty" Rosenthal, Miami, who had the reputation of gambler
and hoodlum associated with other hoodlums and jewel thieves in
the Miami area.

DISPATCH
to
Chief of Station, Caracas
WHO
Chief, WH
FROM
Chief of Station, JIMIAVE
BURGETYETIC/ACLELVE/Oxperimental
D AMICLIVE/15 Report on Arrest of Manuel ESPINOSA Diaz and Two Communist
BETONKOMPEI GUEGFE
Reference: JIMIAVE-8997, 28 Aug 67
1. Attached herewith is ANCLEVE/15's report concerning the
arrest of Manuel *ESPINOSA Diaz and two Communist guerrillas by
DIGEPOL agents on 25 August 1967, the slaying of two Communists
by DIGEPOL agents on 25 August 1967 and ANCLEVE/15's interview
with ESPINOSA.
2. JIMIAVE checked the serial numbers of the weapons as
provided by ANCLEVE/15 in an attempt to determine if they are
of NOFACT/JIMIAVE origin with negative results.
Attachment - h/w
As stated
Distribution
3 - COS, Caracas w/att
2 - C/WI w/o attac fown/3/w
2 - WHI/COG w/att

Chief of Station, Caracas

PHONE
Chief of Station, JMWAVE
SUBJECT TYPICIANCLEVE/Operational
Article/15 Report on Arrest of Manuel ESPINOSA Diaz and Two Communist
ACTION REQUIRED-REFUNCES GUERRILAS
Reference: JMWAVE-8997, 28 Aug 67
1. Attached herewith is ANCLEVE/15's report concerning the
arrest of Manuel "ESPINOSA Diaz and two Communist guerrillas by
DICEPOL agents on 25 August 1967, the slaying of two Communists
by DIEGPOL agents on 25 August 1967 and ANCLEVE/15's interview
with ESPINOSA.
2. JMWAVE checked the serial numbers of the weapons as
provided by ANCLEVE/15 in an attempt to determine if they are
of WOFACT/JHWAVE origin with negative results.
Attachment - h/w
As stated
Distribution
3 - COS, Caracas w/att
2 - C/WH w/o att
2' - WH/COG w/att

ATTACHMENT 01 to UFGA-75432
S E C R E T
MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
MEMORANDUM FOR AMCIEVE/15's Fillo
14 August 1967
SUBJECT: Salary Misunderstanding
ORIGINATOR: Gary L. FLUSTIKOFF
1. ANCLEVE/15 submitted the attached note, written
by him, to the writer. In the note AMCLEVE/15 says
"he is not asking for anything but wants the records checked
regarding his past salary of $325.00 per month. AMCLEVE/15
claimed "Chip" (Grover T'. LUSTICK, 1966, 1968) told
him that effective October 15, 1969, would be paid $300.00.
2. For the record AMCLEVE/15 was told by the writer
and not Chip that effective August 1966 (not October)
he would be cut back in his salary. to approximately
$100.00 per month. lie was cut back from $350.00, not
$325.00, for reasons of economy and cover and ho was
made. The company was not paying $212.00 and the him
that the balance of approximately $212.00 was being
saved for him; only that his gross salary would be
raised to $350.00 in the event RECD ever stopped paying
him his salary. (It was assumed that his RECE employment
was not paid $350.00 in the event RECE paid $350.00
salary cutback was not offective until September 1966 and
from latter date until December 1966 he was paid $111.13.
From January 1967 until June 1967 ho was paid $110.90
due to a FICA change. During the entire period, September
1966, he was paid $110.90. from January 1967 to $110.90
the amount of $330.00 gross with the notation of his
voucher of "possibility of paying balance later". Then
in June 1967 AMCIEVE/15's salary was increased to $350.00
gross, as so promised, because he was uncmployed during
most of Juno.
3. The writer explained the above to AMCLEVE/15
and he seemed satisfied. He told the writer that ho had
to borrow some money to cover expenses in connection
with his trip to Venezuela.

SUBJECT: AMCLEVE/15's Plans for
1 - Registry
Employment - Bona Fides
Given for Possible WOTACT
Contact in the Future
1. AMCLEVE/15 informed the writer on 9 August 1967 the
he plans to fly to Caracas, Venezuela from Miami on 12 August
1967 accompanied by Aldo HERNANDEZ, a friend who is employed
as a salesman in Caracas. In Caracas AMCLEVE/15 will seek
employment through or with an old friend, Ricardo VENTURINE
ska Jose VENTURINE, connected in some way with the TV industry
in Caracas. HERNANDEZ is also a friend of VENTURINE.
2. If AMCLEVE/15 finds employment in Caracas, he does
not intend to return to Miami and his wife and son will then
join him in Caracas.
3. If AMCLEVE/15 does not find employment in Caracas,
he intends to go to Puerto Rico from Caracas to lock for
employment through some of his friends living in Puerto Rico.
4. ANCLEVE/15 was given a recognition signal for estab-
lishing bona fides in the event that MOFACT should want to
contact hin in Caracas or elsewhere. ANCLEVE/15 was instructed
that the person would establish bona fides by saying, "I'm a
friend of Lawrence". Ho was also given JHMAVE address
Mr. Lawrence R. DERONC, PO Box 390, Main Post Office, Miami,
Florida.
5. JHMAVE has no identifiable traces on VENTURINE and
HENRIANDEZ.
6. ANCLEVE/15 reported that his name was mentioned on
the GOC radio on 6 August 1967 in connection with the alleged
captured MOFACT agents. He was described by Alberto LAUCRICA
Diaz as the liaison between WOTACT and REC.

J
DIR 15805 (para 3)
Justice Department has suggested possibility use AMCLEV/15 to assist Rosenthal obtain
additional material as bade for arrest of Rosenthal for having possession of such
materials.
JWAVE 7953 (para-3)
AMCLEVE/15 is currently working with the FBI and followt ng their instructions re
Rosenthal ( 30 June 1967)
DIR 15167
Headquarters will propose to Justice Department that any further questions arising
locally be discussed directly between FBI and Station Rep. (1 July 1967)
JWAVE 8039
At their request JWAVE not with local FBI and Justice Dept. attorney on 6 July
to discuss future action AMCLEVE/15 case. JWAVE position was to agree have
AMCLEVE/15 aid in case as much as possible without exposing AMCLEVE/15 or his
WOPACT employment.
The following proposal:
Justice Dept. attorney requested AMCLEVE/15 recontact Rosenthal and the most would
be covered by FBI. AMCLEVE/15 would ask Rosenthal for money for down payment on
material (e-h explosives) but nothing would nothing would be fumished at that
time. Later AMCLEVE/15 would furnish Rosenthal sufficient amount of explosives
to constitute violation. When AMCLEVE/15 and Rosenthal separated, Rosenthal
vocald be arrested.
AMCLEVE/15 was to contact Alberto Larrain-Maestre and exhibit requested silencer
which would not be fumished. This contact would also be covered by FBI, but
action would be taken by local authorities to avoid possible disclosure as to
involvement of AMCLEVE/15 in the matter.
JWAVE was in process of terminating AMCLEVE/15, but in view of FRI need, he would
be retained on payroll until 30 Sept.


14/00/00
DTR 15094 (dated 7 July 67)
Headquarters opposed toa my use being made of AMCLEVE/15 that would involve his
appearance as a witness for prosecution.
Headquarters requested DMAVE terminate AMCLEVE/15 before permit ting his use
for prosecution. Ex It was Headquarters desire to disassociate from AMCLEVE/15
and have FEL/Justico Dept. assua direction and responsibility for this orininal
case.
JHAYTE 8156 (dated 11 July 67)
Station terminated ANCLEVE/15 effectib 11 Jul67.

FROM
: 10/3/FLUSTIKORF
SUBJECT:
Proposed Termination Bonus
for AMCLEVL/15
1. Pursuant to discussion with DCOS/E and the writer,
JHMAWE plans to terminate AMCL/IV/15 effective 11 July 1967.
2. AMCLEVE/15 began deployment with MCL/ACT during
April 1965 and served as an instructor in the Maritime
Training Section from July 1965 to 1 August 1966 when he
was transferred to the CI Branch. AMCL/VE/15 was used by
the CI Branch to report on the activities of RRCF, a Miami
based Cuban exile group, from 1 August 1966 until above
termination date.
3. Approval is requested for a total of $650.00;
minus PICA and federal income tax. AMCLEVE/15 will be
paid $549.60 net.
APPROVED:
Mark F. EFFIELO
SECRET
S E C R E T
